<div id="s0001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"></div>
<div id="s0002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec-type_intro NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i4" class="section-heading-2">1. Introduction</h2>
 <p>Stochastic optimal control is one of the main subfields of control theory. It is introduced due to considering more realistic models where many systems in different branches of science are subjected to randomness. It is the subject of study in traffic control (Zhong, Sumalee, Pan, &amp; Lam, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0037" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>), airspace industry (Okamoto &amp; Tsuchiya, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0025" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2015</a></span>), cancer chemotherapy (Coldman &amp; Murray, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0010" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2000</a></span>), cyber security systems in computer science (Shang, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0030" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0029" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>), etc. When the system randomness is bounded and the bounds are known, the problem of finding a suitable control action can be dealt with robust control approaches (Doyle, Francis, &amp; Tannenbaum, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0011" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>; Wu &amp; Lee, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0036" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>; Zhou &amp; Doyle, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0038" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1998</a></span>). While the bounds of uncertainty are unknown and the probability distribution of the randomness is available, the stochastic framework should be carried out in optimal control (Åström, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0003" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>; Herzallah, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0018" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Sell, Weinberger, &amp; Fleming, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0028" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1988</a></span>; Touzi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0032" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>). There is a vast amount of literature on stochastic optimal control of linear systems with additive noise where the certainty equivalence property leads to the separation principle in stochastic control (Bar-Shalom &amp; Tse, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0005" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1974</a></span>; Mohammadkhani, Bayat, &amp; Jalali, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0024" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2017</a></span>). Under certain conditions, separation principle asserts that finding a control action for a stochastic system can be restated as designing a stable observer and a stable controller. In the other words, a stochastic problem can be recast as two deterministic problems. Linear quadratic Gaussian control (LQG) is one of the most prominent stochastic control methods. It is simply the combination of Kalman filter as an observer and a linear quadratic controller.</p>
 <p>In spite of much research on the subject of separation principle for nonlinear systems (Atassi &amp; Khalil, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0004" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1999</a></span>; Khalil, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0021" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2008</a></span>), no general separation principle exists for nonlinear systems. Rich theoretical foundations in the literature regarding the deterministic optimal control encourage control engineers to convert stochastic optimal control into a corresponding deterministic one. One approach to remodel a stochastic process into a deterministic counterpart is using Fokker Planck equation (FPE). FPE is a parabolic PDE that models the time evolution of probability density function (PDF) of a stochastic process. PDF of the states of a stochastic process fully characterize the statistical behaviour of the states. Under this scheme, the control function is sought such that the PDF of the states reaches to a desired PDF in time.</p>
 <p>Several studies have been published on stochastic optimal control using FPE in the literature. In Annunziato and Borzì (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0001" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>), the FPE framework for optimal control of the 1-D stochastic process was presented. Finite difference method is utilized for discretization of the OCP. In Annunziato and Borzì (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0002" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>), the authors argued the problem of stochastic optimal control of multidimensional systems and an efficient computational method based on Chang-Cooper scheme was proposed. In Fleig, Grüne, Pesch, and Altmüller (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0014" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>), some theoretical results regarding the existence and uniqueness of the solution of FPE were proved. Also, the existence and uniqueness of the solution of stochastic optimal control using FPE have been investigated; the numerical solution was based on finite difference method. In Annunziato and Borzì (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0001" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0002" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>) and Fleig et al. (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0014" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>), the control function is only the function of time, but in Fleig and Guglielmi, it is assumed to be state dependent as well as time dependent. In Buehler, Paulson, and Mesbah (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0008" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2016</a></span>), a stability constraint was integrated into the FP optimal control in order to guarantee the system stabilization in probability (Battilotti &amp; De Santis, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0006" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>). All the aforementioned papers implement receding horizon control strategy known as model predictive control (MPC) (Camacho &amp; Bordons, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0009" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>; Wang, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0034" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2009</a></span>). To the best of our knowledge, the focus of the literature was not on the numerical discretization of Fokker Planck optimal control.</p>
 <p>The main contribution of this work is on the discretization of the FPE optimal control problem (OCP) using Pseudo-spectral (PS method). PS optimal control is a fast computational method for solving general OCPs. It uses the foundations of PS theory to solve an OCP. The main reason that PS method is suitably fit to the OCPs is: (1) Efficient approximation method for integration in the cost function, solving ODE that governs the dynamic of the system and discretization of the state-space constraint (Fahroo &amp; Ross, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0013" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2008</a></span>; Gong et al., <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0015" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2007</a></span>; Gong, Kang, &amp; Ross, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0016" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2006</a></span>). (2) There is sufficient theoretical support for convergence and consistency of PS method for optimal control based on covector mapping principle (Gong, Ross, Kang, &amp; Fahroo, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0017" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2008</a></span>; Ross, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0026" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2005</a></span>), also PS method is known to be one of the top three numerical solutions of PDEs (Trefethen, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0033" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2000</a></span>). In this paper, instead of approximating ODE that describes the time evolution of the state of the system in a formal PS optimal control framework, we approximate the Fokker Planck PDE which is the dynamical constraint of the stochastic system.</p>
 <p>It would be worth mentioning that not only many theoretical OCP have been solved by PS optimal control, it is also widely applied in practice. It has been successfully implemented in different NASA flight systems (Ross &amp; Karpenko, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0027" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>) and industrial and military applications (Gong et al., <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0015" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2007</a></span>). In this research, we utilize the Legendre PS method (Elnagar, Kazemi, &amp; Razzaghi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0012" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1995</a></span>) based on Legendre-Gauss-Lobatto (LGL) points which is proven to be the most appropriate PS method for solving the finite time OCP with boundary conditions (Fahroo &amp; Ross, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0013" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2008</a></span>). Discretization of FP optimal control yields a large-scale non-linear programming (NLP) which is a hard computational problem. A new intuitive efficient technique based on Genetic algorithm (GA) is adapted to reduce the computational complexity of the NLP.</p>
 <p>The paper is structured as follows: Section <a href="#s0003">2</a> gives a brief review of FPE optimal control with necessary assumptions and the main OCP is determined. PS method fundamentals are described in details in Section <a href="#s0004">3</a>. In Section <a href="#s0005">4</a>, the Methodology of FPE discretization and the proposed method is presented base on GA. Section <a href="#s0006">5</a> gives the numerical results of implementing the proposed method on three benchmark stochastic processes, and finally in Section <a href="#s0007">6</a>, conclusions are provided and future works are described.</p>
</div>
<div id="s0003" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">

 <p><b>Definition 2.2 (The FPE optimal control problem</b>): The Fokker Planck equation optimal control problem is a dynamic optimization problem with PDE constraint, it could be formulated as:</p>

 <p><b>Remark 2</b>: The FPE equation is a second-order PDE, and for solutions we need boundary condition. Condition (5c) is called absorbing boundary condition (Mohammadi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0023" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2015</a></span>). For absorbing boundary condition, the boundaries are chosen such that the probability on the boundaries is zero. The condition (5d) is control constraint condition. Due to physical restrictions in practical systems, the control signals cannot be arbitrary large, so imposing control constraint is necessary for most of OCP.</p>
 <p>The existence of the solution of such OCP with PDE constraints is discussed in (Hinze, Pinnau, Ulbrich, &amp; Ulbrich, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0020" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2008</a></span>).</p>
</div>
<div id="s0004" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i21" class="section-heading-2">3. PS fundamentals</h2>
 <p>PS approximation was initially developed to solve PDEs. In this method, continuous functions are approximated in a finite set of nodes called collocation nodes. These nodes are selected in a way that guarantees the high accuracy of approximation. The main exclusivity of PS method is in the smart selection of collocation nodes. Assume that a real value function <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0029.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0029.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi>
     f
    </mi><mo stretchy="false">
     (
    </mo><mi>
     t
    </mi><mo stretchy="false">
     )
    </mo>
   </math></span> is going to be approximated in <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0030.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0030.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mo stretchy="false">
     [
    </mo><mo>
     −
    </mo><mn>
     1
    </mn><mo>
     ,
    </mo><mn>
     1
    </mn><mo stretchy="false">
     ]
    </mo>
   </math></span> with some interpolants. The simplest but worst choices of nodes are equal distance nodes. But if a special set of nodes such as roots of derivative of Legendre polynomial known as LGL is chosen, the higher accuracy with fewer nodes can be achieved. The following inequality shows the impressive convergence speed of PS method. <disp-formula-group>
   <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_m0009.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_m0009.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div"><span id="m0009" class="disp-formula-label">(6) </span></span></span></span>
   <span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mo>
       |
      </mo>
     </mrow><mrow>
      <mo>
       |
      </mo>
     </mrow><mi>
      f
     </mi><mo stretchy="false">
      (
     </mo><mi>
      t
     </mi><mo stretchy="false">
      )
     </mo><mo>
      −
     </mo><mrow>
      <msub>
       <mi>
        I
       </mi>
       <mi>
        N
       </mi>
      </msub>
     </mrow><mi>
      f
     </mi><mo stretchy="false">
      (
     </mo><mi>

     </mi><mrow>
      <mo stretchy="false">

      </mo>
      <mrow>
       <mo>

      </mrow>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mo>

        </mo>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mrow>
         <msup>
          <mi>

          <mn>

         </msup>
        </mrow>

     </mrow><mo>

     </mo><mrow>
      <mfrac>
       <mi>

       <mrow>

  </disp-formula-group></p>

    </mo><mrow>
     <msup>
      <mi>
       C
      </mi>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       ∞
      </mi>
     </msup>
    </mrow>
   </math></span> <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0038.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0038.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mo stretchy="false">
     (
    </mo><mi>
     m
    </mi><mo>
     =
    </mo><mi mathvariant="normal">
     ∞
    </mi><mo stretchy="false">
     )
    </mo>
   </math></span> the polynomial converges at a spectral rate.</p>
 <p>There are two types of numerical methods to solve an OCP, direct and indirect methods. Indirect methods use the calculus of variation such as Pontryagin minimum principle. These methods are usually hard to solve numerically. Direct methods are known as discretize-then-optimize methods. They are not based on the calculus of variation. In direct methods, the state and control function are approximated by function approximation such as polynomial approximation.</p>
 <p>When an OCP is solved by direct methods, it is highly desirable to use few number of discretization point. A typical OCP consists of three mathematical equations: (1) Integration in the cost function; (2) Differential equation governing the system state evolution; and (3) Algebraic equations appear as the constraints. PS method is suitable for approximation of all three objects. The OCP studied in this paper is different from a typical PS OCP because instead of an ODE constraint, the PDE constraint is utilized which is the FPE.</p>
 <p>There are a lot of theoretical proofs regarding the convergence, consistency and optimality of the solution of PS optimal control. It should be noted that these results are true for systems that are described by the ODE. In this paper, no theoretical proof has been proposed for FP PS optimal control but numerical results prove the validity of the method.</p>
 <p>In this paper, we chose the Gauss PS method with Lagrange interpolant. Since the OCP is finite time, the LGL nodes are used for discretization. Here the necessary foundations of PS method for optimal control are discussed . We show that in PS framework, the differentiations in dynamic constraint of OCP, as well as integration in the cost function can be converted to algebraic equations.</p>

 <div id="s0005-s2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i63">4.1. Genetic algorithm for PS-FP optimal control</h3>
  <p>In this section, we will not discuss the complete procedure of GA algorithm. It is assumed that the reader has basic knowledge about GA. For further information on GA see Whitley (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0035" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1994</a></span>).</p>
  <p>The key steps of the GA-PS-FP optimal control algorithm are as follows:</p>
  <ol class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-order">
   <li><p class="inline">Determine the Maximum iteration, population, percentage of mutation, crossover and other initial parameters of GA.</p></li>
   <li><p class="inline">Consider <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
      <noscript>
       <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0109.gif" alt="">
      </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0109.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
      <math>
       <mrow>
        <msub>
         <mi>
          U
         </mi>
         <mrow>
          <mi>
            
          </mi>
         </mrow>
        </msub>
       </mrow><mo>
        =
       </mo><mo stretchy="false">
        [
       </mo><mi>
        u
       </mi><mo stretchy="false">
        (
       </mo><mrow>
        <msub>
         <mi>
          τ
         </mi>
         <mn>
          0
         </mn>
        </msub>
       </mrow><mo stretchy="false">
        )
       </mo><mo>
        ,
       </mo><mi>
        u
       </mi><mo stretchy="false">
        (
       </mo><mrow>
        <msub>
         <mi>
          τ
         </mi>
         <mn>
          1
         </mn>
        </msub>
       </mrow><mo stretchy="false">
        )
       </mo><mo>
        ,
       </mo><mo>
        .
       </mo><mo>
        .
       </mo><mo>
        .
       </mo><mo>
        ,

  <p>The main advantage of this reformulation of optimization is reducing the number of unknowns to <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0118.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0118.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mi>
      N
     </mi><mo>
      =
     </mo><mrow>
      <msub>
       <mi>
        N
       </mi>
       <mi>
        t
       </mi>
      </msub>
     </mrow><mo>
      +
     </mo><mn>
      1
     </mn>
    </math></span>. Also no NLP should be implemented to find the solution, instead for fitness evaluation a matrix inversion of size <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0119.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0119.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mo stretchy="false">
      (
     </mo><mrow>
      <msub>
       <mi>
        N
       </mi>
       <mi>
        t
       </mi>
      </msub>
     </mrow><mo>
      +
     </mo><mn>
      1
     </mn><mo stretchy="false">
      )
     </mo><mo stretchy="false">
      (
     </mo><mrow>
      <msub>
       <mi>

       </mi>
       <mi>

       </mi>
      </msub>
     </mrow><mo>
      +
     </mo><mn>
      1
     </mn><mo stretchy="false">
      )
     </mo>
    </math></span> must be solved.</p>

<div id="s0006" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i69" class="section-heading-2">5. Simulation results</h2>
 <p>In this section, two stochastic processes are simulated. The proposed algorithm is implemented to find the best control action. Finding the matrix <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0120.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0120.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi mathvariant="normal">
     Ψ
    </mi>
   </math></span>, which might be the most confusing part of the algorithm, is discussed in detail in each example. The interpolated control function is implemented to the SDEs and the Monte-Carlo runs extract the statistical characteristics of states by directly simulation of SDEs using Euler–Maruyama method (Higham, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0019" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2001</a></span>). The Monte-Carlo simulation of SDEs, as well as distance between desired PDF and the PDF of the states, prove the validity of the proposed method.</p>

 <div id="s0006-s2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i72">5.1. Ornstein-Uhlenbleck (OU) process</h3>
  <p>OU Process models the velocity of a massive Brownian particle under influence of friction. It is defined by <disp-formula-group>
    <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_m0040.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_m0040.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div"><span id="m0040" class="disp-formula-label">(32) </span></span></span></span>
    <span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi>
       d
      </mi><mrow>
       <msub>
        <mi>
         X
        </mi>
        <mi>
         t
        </mi>
       </msub>
      </mrow><mo>
       =
      </mo><mo stretchy="false">
       (
      </mo><mo>
       −
      </mo><mi>
       r
      </mi><mrow>
       <msub>
        <mi>
         X
        </mi>
        <mi>
         t
        </mi>
       </msub>
      </mrow><mo>
       +
      </mo><mi>
       U
      </mi><mo stretchy="false">
       )
      </mo><mi>
       d
      </mi><mi>
       t
      </mi><mo>
       +
      </mo><mi>
       σ
      </mi><mi>
       d
      </mi><mrow>
       <msub>
        <mi>
         W
        </mi>
        <mi>
         t
        </mi>
       </msub>
      </mrow>
     </math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div"><span id="m0040" class="disp-formula-label">(32) </span></span></span></span>
   </disp-formula-group></p>
  <p>where <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0121.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0121.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mi>
      X
     </mi>
    </math></span> is the velocity of the particle and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0122.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0122.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mi>
      U
     </mi>
    </math></span> is the momentum due to an external force which is the control action. The simulation parameters are determined in Table <button class="ref showTableEventRef" data-id="t0001">1</button>.</p>

  <p>Figure <a href="#f0001">1</a> shows the distance between desired state PDF and the state PDF under control function and demonstrates the control function at the LGL nodes, also the interpolated control function is calculated by (10). Due to the linearity of the OU process, when the initial distribution is Gaussian, the PDF of the states are always Gaussian. So in order to test the optimal control function, it is implemented on OU and by Monte-Carlo simulations of the SDE in each time step, mean and variance at each time step is calculated. Euler–Maruyama Method is used to solve SDE in each Monte-Carlo run. Figure <a href="#f0002">2</a> compares the mean and variance of the states, obtained by MC simulations and FP equation. LGL points in Figure <a href="#f0002">2</a> represent the discretization points in time. Lagrange interpolation of this points is also demonstrated. It can be seen that the mean and variance obtained by FPE is consistent with MC simulation results. Figure <a href="#f0003">3</a> demonstrates the Barycentric Lagrange interpolation (Berrut &amp; Trefethen, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0007" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2004</a></span>) of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0154.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/oaen20/2019/oaen20.v006.i01/23311916.2019.1691804/20211025/images/oaen_a_1691804_ilm0154.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mi>
      p
     </mi><mo stretchy="false">
      (
     </mo><mi>

     </mi><mo>

  <p>Appendix B shows how to transform (36) to tensor product form. Figures <a href="#f0004">4</a> and <a href="#f0005">5</a> show that for nonlinear system, the proposed method succeeded to find optimal control functions and the FPE solution is consistent with MC simulations. Figure <a href="#f0006">6</a> demonstrates the transient PDF of the typical nonlinear system.</p>

<div id="s0007" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i84" class="section-heading-2">6. Conclusion</h2>
 <p>In this paper, a PS optimal control framework for the stochastic processes is presented. The stochastic optimal control is transformed to OCP by implementing FPE, then discretized in few collocation points by Gauss Legendre spectral discretization Method. In spite of utilizing spectral discretization, the deterministic OCP becomes a large-scaled optimization due to the discretization of FPE which is a PDE. A new technique is represented to solved this large-scaled problem in an efficient way using GA. Two benchmark stochastic processes were simulated and the results prove the validity of the proposed method. The advantages of the proposed method are high accuracy and few computational complexity in comparison with other OCP numerical method for stochastic processes. It is also implementable to nonlinear stochastic processes. The next steps in future researches are as follows:</p>
 <ul class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-bullet">
  <li><p class="inline">Proposing a theoretical framework to prove the optimality and uniqueness of the solution of this method.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Utilizing other PDE numerical techniques such as separation of dimensional domain (Lynch, Rice, &amp; Thomas, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="cit0022" data-reflink="_i85" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1964</a></span>) to solve more than 1-D stochastic process in a reasonable speed.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Advanced numerical technique for large-scale sparse matrix inversion could be implemented to speed up the algorithm.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Instead of GA algorithm, other metaheuristic optimization methods can be utilized to solve the large-scale NLP.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Different choices of collocation points such as Chebyshev or Guass-Lobatto collocation points can be tested and compared together for PS discretization of FPE.</p></li>
 </ul>
 <p></p>
</div>
